@C1
assay: TEXT | An assay based on 10X Genomics. Example : 100x3’ v2 | eg=["10x 3' v3"]
assay_ontology_term_id: TEXT | Experimental Factor Ontology ID (REF: https://www.ebi.ac.uk/ols/ontologies/efo) | eg=["EFO:0009922"]
cell_type_ontology_term_id: TEXT | Cell Ontology ID (i.e. CL:0000784)  (REF: https://www.ebi.ac.uk/ols/ontologies/cl) | eg=["CL:0000066"]
development_stage: TEXT | Human development stage derived from HsapDv term  (Example if data is Homo sapiens, development stage is obtained from Link. HsapDv:0000114 - 20-year-old human stage) | eg=["55-year-old human stage"]
development_stage_ontology_term_id: TEXT | Human Developmental Stages ID (REF: https://www.ebi.ac.uk/ols/ontologies/hsapdv) or Mouse Developmental Stages ID (REF: https://www.ebi.ac.uk/ols/ontologies/mmusdv) (HsapDv if human, MmusDv if mouse, unknown if information unavailable) | eg=["HsapDv:0000149"]
disease: TEXT | Description of disease (example: lung adenocarcinoma) or normal cells | eg=["small cell lung carcinoma"]
disease_ontology_term_id: TEXT | MONDO disease ontology ID (REF: https://www.ebi.ac.uk/ols/ontologies/mondo) (ex. MONDO:0100426 or PATO:0000461 for 'normal') | eg=["MONDO:0008433"]
donor_id: TEXT | Identifies a unique individual that data were derived from | eg=["RU1080"]
feature_biotype: TEXT | Biological type of feature (e.g. gene) | eg=["gene"]
feature_is_filtered: BOOLEAN | Indicates if the feature (gene) was/should be filtered in analysis | eg=[false]
feature_name: TEXT | Gene name from HUGO Human Gene Nomenclature Committee (https://www.genenames.org/) | eg=["KRIT1"]
feature_reference: TEXT | A reference to the feature: NCBI Taxonomy ID | eg=["NCBITaxon:9606"]
is_primary_data: BOOLEAN | Indicates if the sample is primary or not (True/False) | eg=[false]
organism: TEXT | The genus and species from which biosamples are derived | eg=["Homo sapiens"]
organism_ontology_term_id: TEXT | NCBITaxon ID (REF: https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/taxonomy) (ex. NCBITaxon:9606 for human, NCBITaxon:10090 for mouse) | eg=["NCBITaxon:9606"]
self_reported_ethnicity: TEXT | Ethnicity of the individual (obtained from HANCESTRO terms for Homo sapiens) | eg=["European"]
self_reported_ethnicity_ontology_term_id: TEXT | If human, the Human Ancestry Ontology ID (i.e. HANCESTRO:0005) (REF: https://www.ebi.ac.uk/ols/ontologies/hancestro); "multiethnic" if more than one ethnicity. "Unknown" if human and no information, else "na" if non-human | eg=["HANCESTRO:0005"]
sex: TEXT | Phenotypic sex | eg=["female"]
sex_ontology_term_id: TEXT | Phenotype And Trait Ontology ID, PATO:0000384 for male, PATO:0000383 for female, or unknown if unavailable | eg=["PATO:0000383"]
suspension_type: TEXT | Cell, nucleus, or na, as corresponding to sample preparation | eg=["cell"]
tissue_ontology_term_id: TEXT | Uber-anatomy ontology ID (REF: https://www.ebi.ac.uk/ols/ontologies/uberon) (ex.UBERON:2001190) | eg=["UBERON:0002369"]

 locations via vascular channels or lymphatics beyond the regional lymph nodes, using
 criteria established by the American Joint Committee on Cancer (AJCC). | eg=["None"]

 to criteria based on multiple editions of the AJCC's Cancer Staging Manual. | eg=["N1b", "N2a"]

 other parts of the body based on AJCC staging criteria. | eg=["Stage IIIB", "Stage IIIC"]

 primary tumor (T), using staging criteria from the American Joint Committee on Cancer
 (AJCC). | eg=["T3", "T4a"]

Top 10,000 variably accessible peaks (VAPs) were identified using the FindVariableFeatures function in Seurat. We further filtered peaks that were accessible in fewer than 1% of the cells. TF-IDF normalization was then performed on the count matrix with only the VAPs. The PCA was performed on the VAPs and the cells were clustered using the first 50 PCs and the FindClusters function in Seurat with the resolution=0.4. Publication_Abstract: TEXT | The abstract or short description of the content presented/published. | eg=["Colorectal cancers (CRCs) arise from precursor polyps whose cellular origins, molecular heterogeneity, and immunogenic potential may reveal diagnostic and therapeutic insights when analyzed at high resolution. We present a single-cell transcriptomic and imaging atlas of the two most common human colorectal polyps, conventional adenomas and serrated polyps, and their resulting CRC counterparts. Integrative analysis of 128 datasets from 62 participants reveals adenomas arise from WNT-driven expansion of stem cells, while serrated polyps derive from differentiated cells through gastric metaplasia. Metaplasia-associated damage is coupled to a cytotoxic immune microenvironment preceding hypermutation, driven partly by antigen-presentation differences associated with tumor cell-differentiation status. Microsatellite unstable CRCs contain distinct non-metaplastic regions where tumor cells acquire stem cell properties and cytotoxic immune cells are depleted. Our multi-omic atlas provides in..."]
